We are trying to prove the Riemann Hypothesis. A paper draft is attached.

## Your Task: Source-level two-point theorem

Please work only on the **two-point/source-level theorem** in the attached paper draft. Do **not** spend time on the (3)-point or (4)-point branch unless it is strictly needed for this theorem.

### Objective

Try to close the remaining **source-level two-point theorem** that would force the quadratic interaction factorization
[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2,\mathcal J_2,
]
or an equivalent corrected quotient-germ / corrected interaction-remainder statement that gives the same consequence.

I want you to focus on the exact missing source-level structure, not on document cleanup.

### Current state to assume

From the draft, the broad situation is:

* the two-point branch is expected to be settled by a **source-level corrected interaction remainder** or equivalent corrected quotient-germ map;
* the target structure should encode:

  * the right **swap symmetry**,
  * **one-amplitude collapse**,
  * **diagonal collapse**,
  * and the resulting **quadratic ((h_1-h_2)^2)** factor;
* the theorem is expected to rule out the remaining two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches once the factorization is in hand.

### Your job

Please do all of the following:

1. **Locate the exact source-level theorem statement the draft is implicitly aiming at.**
   Rewrite it in the cleanest possible form, ideally as one theorem or proposition.

2. **Audit what is already proved versus missing.**
   Be precise:

   * which identities are already in the draft,
   * which reductions are already valid,
   * which one or two lemmas are actually still open.

3. **Try to prove the missing theorem.**
   If you cannot fully prove it, reduce it as far as possible to a minimal finite list of concrete source identities.

4. **Prefer exact structural formulas over heuristics.**
   I care most about:
   * corrected quotient-germ maps,
   * corrected interaction remainder,
   * symmetry identities,
   * vanishing/collapse identities,
   * factorization mechanisms.

### Routes to attack

Please prioritize these attack routes:

#### Route A: corrected interaction remainder theorem

Try to formulate the exact corrected two-point remainder (\mathcal I_2) or equivalent object whose properties imply
[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2,\mathcal J_2.
]
Then prove:

* swap symmetry,
* one-amplitude collapse,
* diagonal collapse,
* quadratic divisibility.

#### Route B: quotient-germ transport

If the draft is really using a corrected quotient-germ picture, identify the precise map and prove the needed functorial/symmetry/collapse properties there instead of at the scalar remainder level.

#### Route C: minimal finite reduction

If full closure is too hard, reduce the theorem to the smallest possible list of explicit source-level identities. I want exact missing identities, not broad commentary.

### Non-goals

Do **not** spend time on:
* the mixed (4)-point branch,
* the nonmixed (4)-point branch,
* the centered (v_5/u_5)-patch dichotomy,
(these will be worked on in other chats)

So the real target is not another estimate; it is an existence-and-functoriality theorem for the two-atom corrected coefficients themselves.

So the open work is narrower than it first looks: prove presentation invariance/collision for the finite-atomic corrected package, then the rest follows by a short analytic divisibility argument.

So the exact source-level theorem is not merely “there exists an analytic map on atomic sources.” It is:

there exists an analytic source-defined package, normalized at zero, and additive on coincident atoms.

That is the real missing source structure.

Proof

The proof has one genuinely structural step and then a short divisibility argument.
1. The corrected finite-order package is source-defined

The formulas for G\corrG\corr and N\corrN\corr depend only on:
qμ(t±), qμ′(t±), qμ′′(t±), Δμ,m(s),
qμ​(t±​), qμ′​(t±​), qμ′′​(t±​), Δμ,m​(s),

and on the elementary analytic operations appearing in those explicit formulas.

But qμqμ​ and ΦμΦμ​ are linear in μμ. So if two atomic presentations define the same source μμ, they give exactly the same qμqμ​, ΦμΦμ​, Δμ,mΔμ,m​, hence the same corrected same-point blocks and corrected mixed block. Whitening is an analytic function of those blocks on the positive-definite region, so it too depends only on μμ. Therefore every odd coefficient B2k+1,μB2k+1,μ​, and hence
P≤7(μ)=(cμ,A5,μf,A7,μf),
P≤7​(μ)=(cμ​,A5,μf​,A7,μf​),

depends only on μμ.

So the finite-order corrected package is genuinely source-level.
2. Swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, diagonal merger

For two atoms,
μ12=a1δh1+a2δh2.
μ12​=a1​δh1​​+a2​δh2​​.

Since this source is unchanged by swapping the two atoms,
P≤7(a1δh1+a2δh2)=P≤7(a2δh2+a1δh1).
P≤7​(a1​δh1​​+a2​δh2​​)=P≤7​(a2​δh2​​+a1​δh1​​).

That is the exact source-level swap symmetry.

If one amplitude is zero,
a1=0⟹μ12=a2δh2,
a1​=0⟹μ12​=a2​δh2​​,

so
P≤7(μ12)=P≤7(a2δh2),
P≤7​(μ12​)=P≤7​(a2​δh2​​),

and similarly with a2=0a2​=0. That is one-amplitude collapse.

If h1=h2=hh1​=h2​=h, then as atomic sources
a1δh+a2δh=(a1+a2)δh.
a1​δh​+a2​δh​=(a1​+a2​)δh​.

Because P≤7P≤7​ is source-defined,
P≤7(a1δh+a2δh)=P≤7((a1+a2)δh).
P≤7​(a1​δh​+a2​δh​)=P≤7​((a1​+a2​)δh​).

That is the exact diagonal merger identity.

This is the source-level statement the draft was missing.
3. Linearity on one-atom rays

Fix hh, and write
Qh(a):=P≤7(aδh).
Qh​(a):=P≤7​(aδh​).

By the diagonal merger identity,
Qh(a1+a2)=Qh(a1)+Qh(a2).
Qh​(a1​+a2​)=Qh​(a1​)+Qh​(a2​).

Also Qh(0)=0Qh​(0)=0. Since QhQh​ is analytic in aa, the additive Cauchy equation forces linearity:
Qh(a)=a Qh(1).
Qh​(a)=aQh​(1).

Define
Fh:=Qh(1)=P≤7(δh).
Fh​:=Qh​(1)=P≤7​(δh​).

Then
P≤7(aδh)=aFh.
P≤7​(aδh​)=aFh​.

So the draft’s intended decomposition
(two-atom object)=a1Fh1+a2Fh2+(interaction)
(two-atom object)=a1​Fh1​​+a2​Fh2​​+(interaction)

is not an extra axiom. It follows from source-definedness plus diagonal merger.
4. Quadratic factorization of the interaction remainder

Now define
I2(a1,h1;a2,h2):=P≤7(a1δh1+a2δh2)−a1Fh1−a2Fh2.
I2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​):=P≤7​(a1​δh1​​+a2​δh2​​)−a1​Fh1​​−a2​Fh2​​.

By one-amplitude collapse,
I2(0,h1;a2,h2)=0,I2(a1,h1;0,h2)=0.
I2​(0,h1​;a2​,h2​)=0,I2​(a1​,h1​;0,h2​)=0.

Since I2I2​ is analytic, it is divisible by a1a2a1​a2​:
I2(a1,h1;a2,h2)=a1a2 G(h1,h2)
I2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=a1​a2​G(h1​,h2​)

for an analytic GG.

By swap symmetry,
G(h1,h2)=G(h2,h1).
G(h1​,h2​)=G(h2​,h1​).

By diagonal merger and one-atom linearity,
I2(a1,h;a2,h)=P≤7((a1+a2)δh)−a1Fh−a2Fh=(a1+a2)Fh−a1Fh−a2Fh=0.
I2​(a1​,h;a2​,h)=P≤7​((a1​+a2​)δh​)−a1​Fh​−a2​Fh​=(a1​+a2​)Fh​−a1​Fh​−a2​Fh​=0.

Hence
G(h,h)=0.
G(h,h)=0.

Now pass to midpoint/separation variables
m=h1+h22,s=h2−h1,G~(m,s):=G ⁣(m−s2,m+s2).
m=2h1​+h2​​,s=h2​−h1​,G

Swap symmetry makes G~(m,s)G

G~(m,0)=0.
G

G~(m,s)=s2H(m,s)
G

for analytic HH. Returning to (h1,h2)(h1​,h2​),

hence

That proves the source-level two-point factorization.

Replace the current definition block at \label{def:two-pair-decomposition} with:

\begin{definition}[Two-pair decomposition]
\label{def:two-pair-decomposition}
For a normalized two-pair core with amplitudes $a_1,a_2$ and offsets
$h_1,h_2$, write its quotient odd germ schematically as
\[
F_{(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)}(z)
=
a_1F_{h_1}(z)+a_2F_{h_2}(z)+\mathcal I_{12}(z),
\]
where $\mathcal I_{12}(z)$ denotes the pair-interaction germ.

In the explicit finite-order corrected source-level model through order $7$
constructed below, the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic
fixed-sector projections of $\mathcal I_{12}$ are quadratic in the amplitudes
and divisible by $(h_1-h_2)^2$.
\end{definition}

Next, replace the current remark \label{rem:wip-multi-pair-subsection} with:

\begin{remark}[Subsection guide]
\label{rem:wip-multi-pair-subsection}
This subsection is best read as a rigidity program built on the strengthened
one-pair local package
\[
c(h),\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),\qquad \Delta_7(h),
\]
or equivalently the normalized planar curve
\[
h\longmapsto \left(\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}\right).
\]
The projective coincidence conditions remain the organizing principle for the
two-pair and minimal-core analysis. The two-point algebraic interaction
correction is now supplied explicitly below through the source-level
finite-order package, and the remaining steps are the genuine multi-pair
interaction bookkeeping and the extraction into the finite-core endgame.
\end{remark}

Now replace the entire block from

\begin{proposition}[Conditional source-level quadratic interaction remainder]

through the end of the remark

\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}

with the following.

\begin{proposition}[Source-level finite-order quadratic interaction remainder]
\label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
For a small finite atomic source
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
let $q_\mu$ and $\Phi_\mu$ be defined by linear superposition of the corrected
one-pair phase derivative and primitive attached to each atom:
\[
q_\mu:=\sum_j a_j\,q_{h_j},
\qquad
\Phi_\mu:=\sum_j a_j\,\Phi_{h_j}.
\]
Insert $(q_\mu,\Phi_\mu)$ into the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas
of Propositions~\ref{prop:block-perturbation} and
\ref{prop:cross-block-perturbation}, and whiten as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-whitening}. Let
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)
:=
\bigl(c_\mu,\ A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f},\ A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}\bigr)
\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f
\]
denote the resulting cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic
fixed-sector package of the odd germ through order $7$.

For a single atom set
\[
F_h:=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h)
=
\bigl(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),A_7^{\mathfrak f}(h)\bigr).
\]
For two atoms define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]

Then the finite-order source package is source-defined and satisfies
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}+a_1\delta_{h_1}),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]
Moreover there exists an analytic map
\[
\mathcal J_2:\ (\text{small two-atom data})
\longrightarrow
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f
\]
such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
In particular, the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic fixed-sector
interaction defects all satisfy the same quadratic factorization.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By construction, the corrected same-point blocks, the corrected mixed block,
and the whitened block depend on the atomic data only through the source-summed
fields $q_\mu$ and $\Phi_\mu$. Since these are linear in $\mu$, the resulting
finite-order package
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)
=
\bigl(c_\mu,A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f},A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}\bigr)
\]
depends only on the source $\mu$ itself, not on any ordering or presentation of
its atoms. Analyticity in the atomic parameters follows from the linear
superposition in $(q_\mu,\Phi_\mu)$ together with the analytic whitening map of
Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-whitening} after shrinking the source
neighborhood if necessary.

For two atoms, source-definedness immediately gives swap symmetry:
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}+a_1\delta_{h_1}).
\]
Likewise, on the diagonal
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
hence
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h).
\]

Fix $h$ and write
\[
Q_h(a):=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h).
\]
The diagonal merger identity gives
\[
Q_h(a_1+a_2)=Q_h(a_1)+Q_h(a_2).
\]
Since $Q_h$ is analytic in $a$, the analytic Cauchy equation forces linearity:
\[
Q_h(a)=a\,Q_h(1).
\]
Defining
\[
F_h:=Q_h(1)=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h)
\]
yields
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]

Now define
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]
If one amplitude is zero, then by the one-atom linearity just proved,
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Therefore analyticity implies divisibility by $a_1a_2$:
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for an analytic
\[
G:\ (h_1,h_2)\longmapsto \mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f.
\]

Swap symmetry of $\mathfrak P_{\le 7}$ gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]
On the diagonal, using source-definedness and one-atom linearity,
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
(a_1+a_2)F_h-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
0.
\]
Hence
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Pass to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=
G\!\left(m-\frac{s}{2},m+\frac{s}{2}\right).
\]
Because $G$ is symmetric in $(h_1,h_2)$, the function $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is
even in $s$. Since $G(h,h)=0$, we have
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Therefore $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is divisible by $s^2$:
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic $H$. Returning to $(h_1,h_2)$ gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
\]
This proves the proposition.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
Let the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic quotient defects in the
present two-pair section be extracted from the finite-order source package of
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
by the same linear coefficient-extraction and quotient-projection maps used
throughout this subsection. Then on compacta,
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the normalized defects in the present two-pair section are obtained by
dividing by $a_1$, then on normalized families with $|a_2|$ bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first claim is immediate from
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
and the linearity of the coefficient-extraction and quotient-projection maps.

For the normalized defects, divide by $a_1$ and use boundedness of $|a_2|$ on
normalized families. Then
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
O(\delta^2).
\]
On the other hand, on every compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
the second coordinate
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz, since
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta.
\]
Combining the two inequalities gives
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small nonzero $\delta$. Thus the
two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Source-level identities behind the quadratic factor]
\label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}
The proof isolates the exact source-level mechanism behind the two-point
closure. First, coincident-atom merger gives analytic additivity on one-atom
rays:
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]
Thus the two-point interaction remainder is not an extra ansatz: it is the
unique defect of additivity of the finite-order source package on the two-atom
source semigroup. Second, once swap symmetry and diagonal merger are known, the
first nonzero separation term is automatically quadratic:
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
So the two-point source-level theorem is fundamentally a finite-order
source-definedness statement rather than a separate asymptotic estimate.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the strengthened
invariant $\widehat\Psi$, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
together with
Corollary~\ref{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
now close the source-level two-point branch on compact good patches.

Thus the remaining work beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer the
two-point algebraic correction itself. What remains is the genuinely multi-pair
interaction bookkeeping through orders $3,5,7$, together with the local lifted
$3/4$-point analysis for close-point branches on the $v_5\neq 0$ and parallel
$u_5\neq 0$ patches, and the subsequent finite-core extraction.
\end{remark}

Yes — I found one important thing, and it changes the answer.

The main new “finding” is not another goodie. It is that the new source-level proposition is still too strong as written.

The gap is here:
P≤7(a1δh+a2δh)=P≤7((a1+a2)δh)
P≤7​(a1​δh​+a2​δh​)=P≤7​((a1​+a2​)δh​)

does not imply
Qh(a1+a2)=Qh(a1)+Qh(a2).
Qh​(a1​+a2​)=Qh​(a1​)+Qh​(a2​).

So the proof does not actually establish one-atom linearity
P≤7(aδh)=aFh.
P≤7​(aδh​)=aFh​.

And that matters, because the rest of the quadratic factorization proof uses that linearity.

There is a second related issue: the source-summed construction
qμ=∑jajqhj,Φμ=∑jajΦhj
qμ​=j∑​aj​qhj​​,Φμ​=j∑​aj​Φhj​​

is a natural model, but the corrected block formulas are nonlinear in qq and ΦΦ — for example they contain q3q3, sin⁡ΔsinΔ, cos⁡ΔcosΔ, and whitening — so one cannot just read off one-atom linearity from the formulas.

So I would not keep the draft in its current “two-point branch closed” form yet.

What I would do instead is:

    replace the current unconditional source-level proposition by a minimal finite-order criterion lemma, which is true;

    make the two-point source theorem conditional again, but now in a very sharp and useful way;

    update the later “live routes / closed branches” remarks so they no longer claim the two-point branch is finished.

The best real “goodie” to add is this exact minimal criterion.

Replace the current proposition+proof beginning at \label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder} with this:

\begin{lemma}[Minimal finite-order source criterion for quadratic two-point factorization]
\label{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}
Let $V$ be a finite-dimensional complex vector space, and let
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in V
\]
be analytic on a neighborhood of the small two-atom data. Assume that there is
a one-atom package
\[
F_h\in V
\]
such that the following three identities hold:
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},
\qquad
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=a_1F_{h_1},
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
Define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]
Then there exists an analytic map
\[
\mathcal J_2:\ (\text{small two-atom data})\to V
\]
such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By the one-amplitude collapse identities,
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Hence analyticity implies divisibility by $a_1a_2$:
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for an analytic
\[
G:\ (h_1,h_2)\longmapsto V.
\]
Swap symmetry gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]
On the diagonal,
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
(a_1+a_2)F_h-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
0,
\]
so
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]
Now set
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=
G\!\left(m-\frac{s}{2},m+\frac{s}{2}\right).
\]
Since $G$ is symmetric, $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is even in $s$, and since
$G(h,h)=0$, one has
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Therefore $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is divisible by $s^2$:
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2H(m,s)
\]
for analytic $H$. Returning to $(h_1,h_2)$ gives
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
as claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}

admits a source-level realization
\[

\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus

\]
satisfying the three hypotheses of

\bigl(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h)\bigr).
\]
Then on compacta,
\[

\qquad

\qquad

\qquad

\]
If the normalized defects are obtained by dividing by $a_1$, then on normalized
families with $|a_2|$ bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad

\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[

\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}

\end{proof}

Yes — that is the right thing to attack now. I’m checking whether the “diagonal merger” can be proved directly from the corrected block construction already in the paper, rather than assumed as a source-level axiom.

Yes — and the attack immediately reveals something important.

The gap is real, but it is also more structured than it looked. The naive fix “prove
P≤7(aδh)=aFh
P≤7​(aδh​)=aFh​

from the source-summed corrected block formulas” is almost certainly the wrong target.

Here is the decisive computation.

Take a one-atom source of weight aa at height hh. In the attempted source-level construction, you set
qa,h=a qh,Φa,h=a Φh,Δa,h=a Δh.
qa,h​=aqh​,Φa,h​=aΦh​,Δa,h​=aΔh​.

From the explicit corrected same-point formula in Proposition \refprop:block−perturbation\refprop:block−perturbation,
Ga,h,±\corr(s)=1π(2a qh(t±)12a qh′(t±)12a qh′(t±)112(a qh′′(t±)+2a3qh(t±)3)).
Ga,h,±\corr​(s)=π1​(2aqh​(t±​)21​aqh′​(t±​)​21​aqh′​(t±​)121​(aqh′′​(t±​)+2a3qh​(t±​)3)​).

So
Ga,h,±\corr(s)=a Gh,±(a2;s)
Ga,h,±\corr​(s)=aGh,±​(a2;s)​

for some analytic matrix-valued Gh,±Gh,±​.

Likewise, from the explicit corrected mixed block formula in Proposition \refprop:cross−block−perturbation\refprop:cross−block−perturbation, every entry is odd in aa: sin⁡(aΔh)sin(aΔh​) is odd, a qhcos⁡(aΔh)aqh​cos(aΔh​) is odd, and (2−a2q−q+s2)sin⁡(aΔh)(2−a2q−​q+​s2)sin(aΔh​) is odd. Hence
Na,h\corr(s)=a Nh(a2;s)
Na,h\corr​(s)=aNh​(a2;s)​

for some analytic NhNh​.

Now whiten:
Ω^a,h\corr(s)=(Ga,h,−\corr(s))−1/2 Na,h\corr(s) (Ga,h,+\corr(s))−1/2.
Ω
a,h\corr​(s)=(Ga,h,−\corr​(s))−1/2Na,h\corr​(s)(Ga,h,+\corr​(s))−1/2.

Because
Ga,h,±\corr(s)=a Gh,±(a2;s),
Ga,h,±\corr​(s)=aGh,±​(a2;s),

we get
(Ga,h,±\corr(s))−1/2=a−1/2 Gh,±(a2;s)−1/2.
(Ga,h,±\corr​(s))−1/2=a−1/2Gh,±​(a2;s)−1/2.

Therefore the scalar aa cancels:
Ω^a,h\corr(s)=Gh,−(a2;s)−1/2 Nh(a2;s) Gh,+(a2;s)−1/2.
Ω
a,h\corr​(s)=Gh,−​(a2;s)−1/2Nh​(a2;s)Gh,+​(a2;s)−1/2.​

So the raw corrected whitened block depends on aa only through a2a2.

That is the key attack result.

What it means

It means the naive source-summed corrected package is even in the source weight aa, not linear in aa. So the statement
P≤7(aδh)=aFh
P≤7​(aδh​)=aFh​

does not follow from the current block construction, and in fact the construction strongly suggests it is false in that raw form.

So the current “unconditional source-level closure” is not salvageable just by pushing harder on the same proof.

But this also tells us the correct replacement target.

The right theorem to prove is not raw linearity in the source weight. It is a projective one-atom rigidity statement:

for a one-atom source aδhaδh​, the raw finite-order package through order 77 lies on the same line as the normalized one-pair package FhFh​. In other words, one should try to prove
P≤7\raw(aδh)=κ(a,h) Fh
P≤7\raw​(aδh​)=κ(a,h)Fh​​

for some scalar factor κ(a,h)κ(a,h), with the shape FhFh​ independent of aa.

Equivalently, the normalized ratios should be independent of the source weight:
A5,\rawf(a,h)c\raw(a,h)=A5f(h)c(h),Δ7,\raw(a,h)c\raw(a,h)2=Δ7(h)c(h)2.
c\raw​(a,h)A5,\rawf​(a,h)​=c(h)A5f​(h)​,c\raw​(a,h)2Δ7,\raw​(a,h)​=c(h)2Δ7​(h)​.

That is much more plausible, because the draft already treats
Ψ^(h)=(u5(h)c(h),v5(h)c(h),Δ7(h)c(h)2)
Ψ
(h)=(c(h)u5​(h)​,c(h)v5​(h)​,c(h)2Δ7​(h)​)

as the amplitude-invariant object.

So the real attack path is now:

    Prove that the raw one-atom corrected package for aδhaδh​ is projectively constant in aa, not linearly scaling in aa.

    Then for two atoms, work with the raw package in the form

P2\raw(a1,h1;a2,h2)=b1Fh1+b2Fh2+I2,
P2\raw​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=b1​Fh1​​+b2​Fh2​​+I2​,

where bi=κ(ai,hi)bi​=κ(ai​,hi​) are the effective amplitudes.

1. What the ambient two-atom quotient object actually gives

be its class in the ambient odd-germ quotient.

Then three things are true.

First, swap symmetry:
F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)=F2(a2,h2;a1,h1),
F2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=F2​(a2​,h2​;a1​,h1​),

because the source a1δh1+a2δh2a1​δh1​​+a2​δh2​​ is unchanged by swapping the two atoms.

Second, axis collapse:

F2​(a1​,h1​;0,h2​)=Fh1​​,F2​(0,h1​;a2​,h2​)=Fh2​​.

Reason: on an axis the source becomes a single weighted atom, and the weighted one-atom amplitude path is quotient-trivial in \Qabs\Qabs.

Third, diagonal collapse:

F2​(a1​,h;a2​,h)=Fh​.

a1​δh​+a2​δh​=(a1​+a2​)δh​,

again a single weighted atom, hence quotient-equivalent to the normalized one-pair class FhFh​.

3. Obstruction theorem

Here is the clean obstruction.

Assume there exist analytic coefficient functions
λ1,λ2
λ1​,λ2​

defined near (a1,a2)=(0,0)(a1​,a2​)=(0,0), and an analytic remainder
I2(a1,h1;a2,h2)∈\Qabs[[z2]],
I2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)∈\Qabs[[z2]],

such that
F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)=λ1(a1,a2,h1,h2)Fh1+λ2(a1,a2,h1,h2)Fh2+I2(a1,h1;a2,h2),
F2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=λ1​(a1​,a2​,h1​,h2​)Fh1​​+λ2​(a1​,a2​,h1​,h2​)Fh2​​+I2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​),

and such that I2I2​ vanishes on both axes:
I2(a1,h1;0,h2)=0,I2(0,h1;a2,h2)=0.
I2​(a1​,h1​;0,h2​)=0,I2​(0,h1​;a2​,h2​)=0.

Then along the a2=0a2​=0 axis,
F2(a1,h1;0,h2)=Fh1,
F2​(a1​,h1​;0,h2​)=Fh1​​,

so
Fh1=λ1(a1,0,h1,h2)Fh1+λ2(a1,0,h1,h2)Fh2.
Fh1​​=λ1​(a1​,0,h1​,h2​)Fh1​​+λ2​(a1​,0,h1​,h2​)Fh2​​.

Since this must hold for varying h2h2​, one gets
λ1(a1,0,h1,h2)=1,λ2(a1,0,h1,h2)=0.
λ1​(a1​,0,h1​,h2​)=1,λ2​(a1​,0,h1​,h2​)=0.

Similarly, along the a1=0a1​=0 axis,
F2(0,h1;a2,h2)=Fh2,
F2​(0,h1​;a2​,h2​)=Fh2​​,

hence
λ1(0,a2,h1,h2)=0,λ2(0,a2,h1,h2)=1.
λ1​(0,a2​,h1​,h2​)=0,λ2​(0,a2​,h1​,h2​)=1.

But now λ1λ1​ would have to satisfy
λ1(a1,0,… )=1for all small a1,λ1(0,a2,… )=0for all small a2,
λ1​(a1​,0,…)=1for all small a1​,λ1​(0,a2​,…)=0for all small a2​,

which is impossible for a function analytic at (0,0)(0,0). The same contradiction appears for λ2λ2​.

So:
there is no analytic ambient-quotient decomposition with axis-vanishing remainder near (a1,a2)=(0,0).
there is no analytic ambient-quotient decomposition with axis-vanishing remainder near (a1​,a2​)=(0,0).​

That is the key result of this attack.
4. What this means

This shows that the direct quotient-germ route is too quotientized.

So the remaining source-level theorem is not going to come from a pure \Qabs\Qabs-valued two-atom object alone.

The two-point theorem must live in a lift of the ambient quotient, not in \Qabs\Qabs itself.

More concretely, you need a finite-order object that still remembers the external source coefficients at the cubic/quintic/septic levels. That is exactly why the draft’s finite-order corrected package

    Still plausible and necessary: a lifted finite-order source-sensitive package through orders 3,5,73,5,7.

The no-go theorem

Then each component is an even analytic function of aa.

In particular,
ca(h),A5,af(h),A7,af(h)

all depend on aa through a2a2.
Proof

Ga,h,±\corr(s)=1π(2a qh(t±)12a qh′(t±)12a qh′(t±)112(a qh′′(t±)+2a3qh(t±)3)).

a1, a2
a1​, a2​

So any replacement theorem must still produce a lift with those external source coefficients, or something demonstrably equivalent.

The current source-summed package does not do that.

the present source-summed corrected finite-order model cannot prove the desired two-point source theorem.

The NN-point cancellation package is also mostly indirect for this exact attack. Here is the clean statement.
Proposition (exact close two-point exclusion from quotient diagonal collapse)

Let
F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)∈\Qabs[[z2]]
F2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)∈\Qabs[[z2]]

denote the actual corrected quotient odd germ attached to the normalized two-atom data (a1,h1;a2,h2)(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​).

Assume:

    F2F2​ is continuous in the normalized two-atom parameters;

    on the diagonal,

F2(a1,h;a2,h)=Fh,
F2​(a1​,h;a2​,h)=Fh​,

where FhFh​ is the normalized one-pair quotient germ;

    on J⋐{c≠0}J⋐{c=0}, one has Fh≠0Fh​=0.

Then there exists εJ>0εJ​>0 such that no normalized bad two-pair core with
h1,h2∈J,0<∣h1−h2∣<εJ
h1​,h2​∈J,0<∣h1​−h2​∣<εJ​

can exist.
Proof

Assume the contrary. Then there is a sequence of normalized bad two-pair cores
(a1(n),h1(n);a2(n),h2(n))
(a1(n)​,h1(n)​;a2(n)​,h2(n)​)

with
h1(n),h2(n)∈J,h1(n)−h2(n)→0,
h1(n)​,h2(n)​∈J,h1(n)​−h2(n)​→0,

and
F2(a1(n),h1(n);a2(n),h2(n))=0
F2​(a1(n)​,h1(n)​;a2(n)​,h2(n)​)=0

because they are bad cores.

By compactness of JJ and the normalization on amplitudes, after passing to a subsequence we may assume
h1(n)→m,h2(n)→m,a1(n)→a1∗,a2(n)→a2∗.
h1(n)​→m,h2(n)​→m,a1(n)​→a1∗​,a2(n)​→a2∗​.

Continuity of F2F2​ gives
0=lim⁡n→∞F2(a1(n),h1(n);a2(n),h2(n))=F2(a1∗,m;a2∗,m).
0=n→∞lim​F2​(a1(n)​,h1(n)​;a2(n)​,h2(n)​)=F2​(a1∗​,m;a2∗​,m).

Now apply diagonal collapse:
F2(a1∗,m;a2∗,m)=Fm.
F2​(a1∗​,m;a2∗​,m)=Fm​.

Hence
Fm=0.
Fm​=0.

But m∈J⋐{c≠0}m∈J⋐{c=0}, so the one-pair quotient germ is nonzero there. Contradiction.

So such a sequence cannot exist.

Verdict: the argument is mathematically sound as a conditional bypass, but it does not yet check out as an unconditional theorem of the draft.

What does check out is the internal logic of the contradiction:

If you had a genuine corrected two-atom quotient map
F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)∈\Qabs[[z2]]
F2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)∈\Qabs[[z2]]

defined on normalized two-atom data, continuous in those parameters, and satisfying exact diagonal collapse
F2(a1,h;a2,h)=Fh,
F2​(a1​,h;a2​,h)=Fh​,

then the close exact two-point bad-core exclusion argument is fine. Combined with “bad core means quotient odd germ vanishes identically,” it would rule out exact bad two-point cores accumulating to the diagonal on compact patches where Fh≠0Fh​=0.

The parts that already match the draft are these.

The one-pair quotient germ FhFh​ is a real object in the draft. “Bad normalized finite core” is defined by vanishing of its quotient odd germ. And on the good one-pair region the cubic leading coefficient is nonzero, so on a patch J⋐{c≠0}J⋐{c=0}, the one-pair germ is certainly not the zero germ. So the contradiction endpoint
0=F2(⋯ )→Fm≠0
0=F2​(⋯)→Fm​=0

is the right shape.

What does not currently check out is the input package needed to run that proof.

First, the draft does not presently define the actual two-atom quotient object F2F2​ in a theorem-strength way. The current def:two-pair-decomposition is explicitly schematic, and it is phrased in exactly the amplitude-linear way that we have already found reason to distrust.

Second, the draft does not yet prove continuity of the quotient germ for a normalized two-atom family in the atomic parameters. That continuity is plausible, but right now it is not a proved lemma.

Third, the diagonal collapse
F2(a1,h;a2,h)=Fh
F2​(a1​,h;a2​,h)=Fh​

is also not a proved theorem in the current text. It would need a genuine source-to-quotient functoriality statement for coincident atoms, plus the claim that the weighted one-atom path is quotient-trivial in the relevant sense. Architecturally that is plausible, but it is not yet established in the draft.

Fourth, your compactness step on amplitudes also needs one more explicit input. I do not see a standalone theorem in the current draft stating that the normalized two-point amplitude space is compact or precompact. If normalization really fixes the amplitudes up to a compact projective parameter, then the subsequence extraction is fine. But that assumption still needs to be made explicit.

So the cleanest summary is:

Your bypass is a good conditional proposition, not yet a proved replacement theorem.

More specifically, it proves the following conditional statement:

If the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ exists as a continuous function of normalized two-atom data and collapses on the diagonal to the one-pair quotient germ, then exact close bad two-point cores cannot occur on compact patches J⋐{c≠0}J⋐{c=0}.

That is worth keeping. It is substantially weaker than the current source-level quadratic factorization target, but also much more believable.

Two caveats matter.

It only kills the exact close two-point bad-core branch. It does not recover the current quantitative defect machinery.

And it does not yet integrate automatically with the present two-pair subsection, because that subsection is still organized around defect identities and the conditional finite-order source criterion.

So my honest recommendation is: do not replace the current two-point bottleneck by this as if it were done. But it is definitely worth recording as a sharper alternative route, conditional on a much smaller input package than the false source-linear theorem.

The next step would be to state it in the draft explicitly as a conditional exact two-point exclusion proposition, rather than as a claimed closure.

Yes. I would add this as a separate conditional bypass, not as a replacement for the current source-level criterion.

Insert the following block immediately after the proof of

\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}

and before \begin{remark}[Exact remaining source-level input on the two-point branch].

\begin{proposition}[Conditional exact two-point exclusion from quotient diagonal collapse]
\label{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs}
Let
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}
\]
be a compact interval. Assume there exists an actual corrected two-atom quotient
map
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \Qabs[[z^2]]
\]
defined on normalized two-pair data, with the following properties:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Continuity.}
The map $\mathcal F_2$ is continuous in the normalized two-pair parameters.

\item \textbf{Diagonal collapse.}
For every $h\in J$ and every normalized amplitude pair $(a_1,a_2)$,
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h,
\]
where $F_h$ is the normalized one-pair quotient odd germ.

\item \textbf{Precompactness of normalized amplitudes.}
Every sequence of normalized two-pair data with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0
\]
admits a subsequence along which the full normalized parameter tuple converges.
\end{enumerate}

Then there is no sequence of nontrivial normalized bad two-pair cores
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
\]
with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
Equivalently, under the three assumptions above, the exact close two-point
bad-core branch is excluded on compact subsets of $\{c\neq 0\}$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assume for contradiction that there exists a sequence of nontrivial normalized
bad two-pair cores
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
\]
with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
Since each core is bad, its quotient odd germ vanishes identically, so
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})=0
\qquad
\text{for all }n.
\]

By the precompactness assumption, after passing to a subsequence we may assume
that the full normalized parameter tuple converges:
\[
a_{1,n}\to a_1^*,
\qquad
a_{2,n}\to a_2^*,
\qquad
h_{1,n}\to m,
\qquad
h_{2,n}\to m
\]
for some $m\in J$. By continuity of $\mathcal F_2$,
\[
0
=
\lim_{n\to\infty}
\mathcal F_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
=
\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
Applying diagonal collapse gives
\[
0=\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)=F_m.
\]

But $m\in J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}$, so the normalized one-pair quotient germ
$F_m$ is nonzero: its cubic leading coefficient is nonzero on $\{c\neq 0\}$.
This contradiction proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[A weaker exact two-point route]
\label{rem:weaker-exact-two-point-route}
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs} is strictly
weaker than the quadratic defect-factorization route of
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}. It does not produce
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
and does not yield the quantitative defect estimates used in
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}.
Instead, it isolates a smaller alternative input: a genuine corrected two-atom
quotient map, continuity in normalized parameters, and exact diagonal collapse
to the one-pair quotient class.

Thus there are now two distinct two-point routes in the draft:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the stronger finite-order source-level route, which would force quadratic
defect bounds and hence quantitative defect-scale closeness;

\item the weaker quotient-diagonal route, which would already exclude exact
close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of $\{c\neq 0\}$.
\end{enumerate}

At present, the draft does not prove either route outright. The first remains a
finite-order source-level merger problem; the second remains a continuity and
diagonal-collapse problem for the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ.
\end{remark}

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a
vague interaction heuristic.

with:

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a
vague interaction heuristic. There are now two precise conditional routes on the
two-point side: the stronger finite-order source-level merger route, which

The most important point is not that the 3-point or nonmixed 4-point results directly solve the 2-point bottleneck. They do not. The note is still right that the live 2-point obstruction remains the source-level reduction/factorization in the two-pair block.

What has changed is the language that now looks most promising.

First, the nonmixed 4-point source-determinant picture is a real methodological clue. The draft now treats repeated-source 4-point geometry via a finite ratio of source determinants, and the derivative of that ratio is controlled by a single 4×44×4 source determinant. That strongly suggests that for the mixed side too, the right “below-lifted” variables may be finite source minors and their sign/ratio behavior, rather than raw lifted coordinates alone. That is exactly the kind of structure I had been groping toward with the failed source-linear and blow-up attacks, but this is a better-organized version of it.

Second, the no-go lemma about (x,S)(x,S)-only geometry is strategically important well beyond the nonmixed route. It says that no argument using only planar (x,S)(x,S) geometry can exclude the relevant degeneracies; any successful mixed closure must use extra coupling — parity transfer, patch dichotomy, or genuine source-level coupling between the YY- and SS-channels. That is very relevant to the 2-point attack, because it tells us why several of my recent “purely geometric” or “continuity-only” bypasses were too weak. They were trying to win without enough channel coupling.

Third, the first-loss rigidification remark is useful as a template. In the nonmixed case, first loss of quadratic-envelope monotonicity rigidifies into a sheared repeated-node tangency mechanism. That is not a proof for the mixed side, but it suggests a better local question: when mixed two-point or four-point monotonicity first fails, does it rigidify into a lower-core tangency profile that can be recognized source-level? That is much sharper than the broad “prove quadratic factorization somehow” target. This is especially appealing because the 3-point branch is now more derivative-geometric and less ad hoc, via the osculating determinant and the global continuation theorem.

Fourth, the Jm(λ)Jm​(λ) odd/even local-classification template is probably reusable once parity is transferred into the actual mixed coordinate. I would not say it solves the 2-point problem, but it does suggest that once you have the right source-minor variable or regularized mixed profile, the three low-order obstruction types may need to be attacked one by one with weighted-average / implicit-function arguments, rather than through one giant source theorem.

So my updated assessment is:

The new 3-point and nonmixed 4-point progress does not rescue the old two-point routes I already broke.

But it does point to the best new route:

work in a source-minor / ratio language, not a raw lifted-variable language, and make sure the object still carries genuine YY-SS coupling.

That means the best next attack on the 2-point branch is no longer:

The best next attack is:

find a finite source-determinant package for the two-point mixed defect channels — at minimum for the cubic/quintic strengthened data — whose vanishing or sign behavior detects the close collision-cancellation branch.

In plainer terms: try to build for the 2-point branch the analogue of the nonmixed ΨaΨa​ / D(a,h)D(a,h) package, but now for the mixed strengthened channels. If that object exists, it is much more likely to yield the missing source-level reduction than the approaches I was trying earlier.

Here is the exact reason.

Let
A5,i:=A5f(hi),A7,i:=A7f(hi),
A5,i​:=A5f​(hi​),A7,i​:=A7f​(hi​),

and on an exact bad two-pair core write
A5,1=λA5,2.
A5,1​=λA5,2​.

The draft’s projected septic gauge law is
A7,i↦A7,i+βiA5,i,
A7,i​↦A7,i​+βi​A5,i​,

and the raw representative is explicitly described as noncanonical, with only local auxiliary gauge-fixes like v7=0v7​=0 or u7=0u7​=0 on a patch. The handoff note is also still consistent with the two-point bottleneck being source-level rather than already closed.

Now define the pre-quotient two-point septic difference
Ξ:=A7,1−λA7,2.
Ξ:=A7,1​−λA7,2​.

Under independent gauges at the two points,
Ξ↦Ξ+β1A5,1−λβ2A5,2=Ξ+(β1−β2)A5,1.
Ξ↦Ξ+β1​A5,1​−λβ2​A5,2​=Ξ+(β1​−β2​)A5,1​.

So if you decompose ΞΞ relative to A5,1A5,1​ as
Ξ=L A5,1+T JA5,1,
Ξ=LA5,1​+TJA5,1​,

then
T is invariant,L↦L+(β1−β2).
T is invariant,L↦L+(β1​−β2​).

That is the decisive obstruction.

The transverse coefficient TT is exactly the quotient-visible part, equivalently the determinant part already encoded by Δ7Δ7​ or the septic quotient class. But the longitudinal coefficient LL is completely gauge-dependent: by choosing β1−β2β1​−β2​ arbitrarily, you can shift LL arbitrarily.

So there is no intrinsic theorem about LL available from the present quotient package alone.

That also explains why the local gauge-fixing remark in the draft does not rescue this route. On a v5≠0v5​=0 patch, setting v7=0v7​=0 gives
u7\new=Δ7v5,
u7\new​=v5​Δ7​​,

and on a u5≠0u5​=0 patch, setting u7=0u7​=0 gives
v7\new=−Δ7u5.
v7\new​=−u5​Δ7​​.

But those are just pointwise gauge sections for the already quotient-visible septic data. They do not canonically compare two different points, and they do not produce a shear-sensitive invariant beyond what Δ7Δ7​ already sees.

So the current attack yields a stronger no-go statement than before:
The present cubic/quintic source minors plus the septic quotient class see only the transverse part of Ξ, never the longitudinal part.
The present cubic/quintic source minors plus the septic quotient class see only the transverse part of Ξ, never the longitudinal part.​

Equivalently:
Any proof that only uses the existing quotient-level septic machinery is exactly blind to the repeated-node shear.
Any proof that only uses the existing quotient-level septic machinery is exactly blind to the repeated-node shear.​

That is now the clean structural fact.

What this means for the next attack is also clearer.

A successful mixed two-point argument must add one extra ingredient that couples the gauges at h1h1​ and h2h2​. There are only two realistic ways I can see:

First, a pre-quotient transport law.
You would need a canonically chosen smooth gauge section along a patch, not just pointwise gauge-fixing. Then the difference
Ξ♯=A7,1♯−λA7,2♯
Ξ♯=A7,1♯​−λA7,2♯​

would become meaningful, and its longitudinal component could carry the shear.

Second, a parity-transferred mixed local model.
Instead of comparing raw septic representatives directly, you build a repeated-node normal form in the actual mixed coordinate, where the shear appears as a genuine coefficient before quotienting ever happens.

Of those two, the first now looks like the sharpest theorem to target:

and those are exactly the affine coordinates of the secant shadow of the pair (h1,h2)(h1​,h2​) on the plane S=0S=0:
Σ(h1,h2)=(x1S2−x2S1S2−S1, Y1S2−Y2S1S2−S1).
Σ(h1​,h2​)=(S2​−S1​x1​S2​−x2​S1​​, S2​−S1​Y1​S2​−Y2​S1​​).

The projective version is the cleaner invariant:
Σ(h1,h2)=[x1S2−x2S1: Y1S2−Y2S1: S2−S1].
Σ(h1​,h2​)=[x1​S2​−x2​S1​: Y1​S2​−Y2​S1​: S2​−S1​].​

As h2→h1=ah2​→h1​=a, this converges to the projective tangent shadow
Π(a)=[x(a)S′(a)−S(a): Y(a)S′(a)−S(a)Y′(a): S′(a)].
Π(a)=[x(a)S′(a)−S(a): Y(a)S′(a)−S(a)Y′(a): S′(a)].​

That is the first genuinely robust geometric object I trust.

Now the useful new fact:

If you differentiate ΠΠ, a short computation gives
Π(a)∧Π′(a)=S(a) ( S′(a)Y′′(a)−S′′(a)Y′(a), S′′(a), ∗ ).
Π(a)∧Π′(a)=S(a)(S′(a)Y′′(a)−S′′(a)Y′(a), S′′(a), ∗).

So the second component is
S(a) S′′(a).
S(a)S′′(a).

Hence the projective tangent-shadow map is immersive whenever
S(a)≠0andS′′(a)≠0.
S(a)=0andS′′(a)=0.

Because on a good v5v5​-patch the draft already identifies
Kv=(x′)3S′′,
Kv​=(x′)3S′′,

this means:
Π is projectively immersive away from {S=0}∪{Kv=0}.
Π is projectively immersive away from {S=0}∪{Kv​=0}.​

That is a genuine improvement over my earlier reduction. It removes the spurious exceptional slice
{S′=0}
{S′=0}

entirely. Projective compactification regularizes it.

So the mixed 2-point branch is now reduced to two explicit geometric accumulation loci:
{S=0}or{Kv=0}.
{S=0}or{Kv​=0}.​

That lines up much better with the current draft than the older S′S′-based formulations. The 2-point burden is still source-level, while the KvKv​-branch is already one of the mature derivative-geometric parts of the paper.

What this does not yet prove is exclusion. A family of secant-shadow points can still converge to a tangent shadow point without forcing a contradiction. So this is not closure.

But it is a better reduction:

    the exact invariant is the projective secant-shadow Σ(h1,h2)Σ(h1​,h2​), not the affine ΦΦ-map;

    the only remaining geometric exceptional loci are S=0S=0 and Kv=0Kv​=0;

    so the next attack should split exactly there.

The best next steps are now:

    prove that accumulation on Kv=0Kv​=0 is absorbed by the existing lifted 3-point branch, which the current draft already treats as the derivative-geometric locus for shrinking exact lifted 3-point circuits;

    analyze the septic-zero slice

S=Δ7c v5=0
S=cv5​Δ7​​=0

and show that a close mixed 2-point branch cannot accumulate there without already entering the existing mixed low-order obstruction framework.

So the branch is not closed, but the geometry is cleaner now than before.
